  </h1>\n   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">\n    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">\n     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia\n    </div>\n    <div id="contentSub">\n    </div>\n the NASA launch facility located on Merritt Island. colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #efefef">\n         Map\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n         <a class="image" style="display:none">\n        <th colspan="2">\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #efefef">\n         Footnotes\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">\n          <a href="#cite_note-1">\n           [1]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <b>\n        John F. Kennedy Space Center\n       </b>\n       (\n       <b>\n        KSC\n       </b>\n       ) is one of ten\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n        National Aeronautics and Space Administration\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA_facilities#NASA_field_centers" title="NASA facilities">\n        field centers\n       </a>\n       . Since December 1968, Kennedy Space Center has been NASA\'s primary launch center of human spaceflight. Launch operations for the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apollo_Program" title="Apollo Program">\n        Apollo\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Skylab" title="Skylab">\n        Skylab\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Program" title="Space Shuttle Program">\n        Space Shuttle\n       </a>\n       programs were carried out from\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39" title="Kennedy Space Center Launch Complex 39">\n        Kennedy Space Center Launch Complex 39\n       </a>\n       and managed by KSC.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Located on the east coast of Florida, KSC is adjacent to\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Canaveral_Air_Force_Station" title="Cape Canaveral Air Force Station">\n        Cape Canaveral Air Force Station\n       </a>\n       (CCAFS). The management of the two entities work very closely together, share resources, and even own facilities on each other\'s property.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Though the first Apollo flights, and all\n       <a href="/wiki/Project_Mercury" title="Project Mercury">\n        Project Mercury\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Project_Gemini" title="Project Gemini">\n        Project Gemini\n       </a>\n       flights took off from CCAFS, the launches were managed by KSC and its previous organization, the Launch Operations Directorate.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Starting with the fourth Gemini mission, the NASA launch control center in Florida (\n       <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Control_Center" title="Mercury Control Center">\n        Mercury Control Center\n       </a>\n       , later the\n       <a href="/wiki/Launch_Control_Center" title="Launch Control Center">\n        Launch Control Center\n       </a>\n       ) began handing off control of the vehicle to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_C._Kraft_Jr._Mission_Control_Center" title="Christopher C. Kraft Jr. Mission Control Center">\n        Mission Control Center\n       </a>\n       shortly after liftoff; in prior missions it held control throughout the entire mission.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lipartito_6-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Lipartito-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Additionally, the center manages launch of robotic and commercial crew missions, researches food production and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/In-Situ_Resource_Utilization" title="In-Situ Resource Utilization">\n        In-Situ Resource Utilization\n       </a>\n       for off Earth exploration,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Research_.26_Tech_7-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Research_.26_Tech-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and more. Since 2010, the center has worked to become a multi-user\n       <a href="/wiki/Spaceport" title="Spaceport">\n        spaceport\n       </a>\n       through industry partnerships,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       even adding a new launch pad (\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39#Launch_Pad_39C" title="Kennedy Space Center Launch Complex 39">\n        LC-39C\n       </a>\n       ) in 2015.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There are about 700 facilities grouped across the center\'s 144,000 acres.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Master_Plan_2012_9-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Master_Plan_2012-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Among the unique facilities at KSC are the 525\xc2\xa0ft tall\n       <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_Assembly_Building" title="Vehicle Assembly Building">\n        Vehicle Assembly Building\n       </a>\n       for stacking NASA\'s largest rockets, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Operations_and_Checkout_Building" title="Operations and Checkout Building">\n        Operations and Checkout Building\n       </a>\n       , which houses the astronaut crew quarters, and 3-mile-long\n       <a href="/wiki/Shuttle_Landing_Facility" title="Shuttle Landing Facility">\n        Shuttle Landing Facility\n       </a>\n       . There is also a\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center_Visitor_Complex" title="Kennedy Space Center Visitor Complex">\n        Visitor Complex\n       </a>\n       open to the public on site.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li tocsection-12">\n           <a href="#Payload_processing">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Payload processing\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13">\n           <a href="#Launch_Complex_39">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Launch Complex 39\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14">\n           <a href="#Commercial_leasing">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Commercial leasing\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15">\n           <a href="#Visitor_complex">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Visitor complex\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16">\n           <a href="#Historic_locations">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.5\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Historic locations\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17">\n         <a href="#Weather">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           6\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Weather\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18">\n         <a href="#KSC_directors">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           7\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           KSC directors\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19">\n         <a href="#Labor_force">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           8\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Labor force\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           9\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           10\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22">\n         <a href="#Bibliography">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           11\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Bibliography\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           12\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Formation">\n        Formation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Formation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The military had been performing launch operations since 1949 at what would become\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Canaveral_Air_Force_Station" title="Cape Canaveral Air Force Station">\n        Cape Canaveral Air Force Station\n       </a>\n       . In December 1959, the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">\n        Department of Defense\n       </a>\n       transferred 5,000 personnel and the Missile Firing Laboratory to\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n        NASA\n       </a>\n       to become the Launch Operations Directorate under NASA\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Space_Flight_Center" title="Marshall Space Flight Center">\n        Marshall Space Flight Center\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       President\n       <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">\n        John F. Kennedy\n       </a>\n       \'s 1961 goal of a manned lunar landing before 1970 required an expansion of launch operations. On July 1, 1962, the Launch Operations Directorate was separated from MSFC to become the\n       <b>\n        Launch Operations Center (LOC).\n       </b>\n       Also, Cape Canaveral was inadequate to host the new launch facility design required for the mammoth 363-foot (111\xc2\xa0m) tall, 7,500,000-pound-force (33,000\xc2\xa0kN) thrust\n       <a href="/wiki/Saturn_V" title="Saturn V">\n        Saturn V\n       </a>\n       rocket, which would be assembled vertically in a large hangar and transported on a mobile platform to one of several launch pads. Therefore, the decision was made to build a new LOC site located adjacent to Cape Canaveral on\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merritt_Island" title="Merritt Island">\n        Merritt Island\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       NASA began land acquisition in 1962, buying title to 131 square miles (340\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) and negotiating with the state of Florida for an additional 87 square miles (230\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MOONPORT5-11_10-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MOONPORT5-11-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The major buildings in KSC\'s Industrial Area were designed by architect\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Luckman" title="Charles Luckman">\n        Charles Luckman\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Construction began in November 1962, and Kennedy visited the site twice in 1962, and again just a week before\n       <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_John_F._Kennedy" title="Assassination of John F. Kennedy">\n        his assassination\n       </a>\n       on November 22, 1963.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KSC_History_Quiz_12-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-KSC_History_Quiz-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On November 29, 1963, the facility was given its current name by President Lyndon B. Johnson under\n       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Executive_Order_11129" title="s:Executive Order 11129">\n        Executive Order 11129\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KSC_Story_14-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-KSC_Story-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Johnson\'s order joined both the civilian LOC and the military Cape Canaveral station ("the facilities of Station No. 1 of the Atlantic Missile Range") under the designation "John F. Kennedy Space Center", spawning some confusion joining the two in the public mind. NASA Administrator\n       <a href="/wiki/James_E._Webb" title="James E. Webb">\n        James E. Webb\n       </a>\n       clarified this by issuing a directive stating the\n       <i>\n        Kennedy Space Center\n       </i>\n       name applied only to the LOC, while the Air Force issued a general order renaming the military launch site\n       <i>\n        Cape Kennedy Air Force Station\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moonport_appendixb_15-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Moonport_appendixb-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Location">\n        Location\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Location">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Located on\n       <a href="/wiki/Merritt_Island,_Florida" title="Merritt Island, Florida">\n        Merritt Island, Florida\n       </a>\n       , the center is north-northwest of\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Canaveral" title="Cape Canaveral">\n        Cape Canaveral\n       </a>\n       on the Atlantic Ocean, midway between Miami and\n       <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville,_Florida" title="Jacksonville, Florida">\n        Jacksonville\n       </a>\n       on Florida\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Coast" title="Space Coast">\n        Space Coast\n       </a>\n       , due east of\n       <a href="/wiki/Orlando,_Florida" title="Orlando, Florida">\n        Orlando\n       </a>\n       . It is 34 miles (55\xc2\xa0km) long and roughly six miles (9.7\xc2\xa0km) wide, covering 219 square miles (570\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       KSC is a major central Florida\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tourist_destination" title="Tourist destination">\n        tourist destination\n       </a>\n       and is approximately one hour\'s drive from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Orlando,_Florida" title="Orlando, Florida">\n        Orlando\n       </a>\n       area. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center_Visitor_Complex" title="Kennedy Space Center Visitor Complex">\n        Kennedy Space Center Visitor Complex\n       </a>\n       offers public tours of the center and Cape Canaveral Air Force Station.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Because much of the installation is a restricted area and only nine percent of the land is developed, the site also serves as an important\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wildlife_sanctuary" title="Wildlife sanctuary">\n        wildlife sanctuary\n       </a>\n       ;\n       <a href="/wiki/Mosquito_Lagoon" title="Mosquito Lagoon">\n        Mosquito Lagoon\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Indian_River_(Florida)" title="Indian River (Florida)">\n        Indian River\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Merritt_Island_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="Merritt Island National Wildlife Refuge">\n        Merritt Island National Wildlife Refuge\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Canaveral_National_Seashore" title="Canaveral National Seashore">\n        Canaveral National Seashore\n       </a>\n       are other features of the area. Center workers can encounter\n       <a href="/wiki/Bald_eagle" title="Bald eagle">\n        bald eagles\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/American_alligator" title="American alligator">\n        American alligators\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Razorback" title="Razorback">\n        wild boars\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crotalus_adamanteus" title="Crotalus adamanteus">\n        eastern diamondback rattlesnakes\n       </a>\n       , the endangered\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida_panther" title="Florida panther">\n        Florida panther\n       </a>\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2015)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Indian_manatee" title="West Indian manatee">\n        Florida manatees\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_programs">\n        Historical programs\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Historical programs">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Apollo_program">\n        Apollo program\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Apollo program">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">\n        Apollo program\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Apollo_missions" title="List of Apollo missions">\n        List of Apollo missions\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Saturn_V_aerial.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1034" data-file-width="783" height="224" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f0/Saturn_V_aerial.jpg/170px-Saturn_V_aerial.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f0/Saturn_V_aerial.jpg/255px-Saturn_V_aerial.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f0/Saturn_V_aerial.jpg/340px-Saturn_V_aerial.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Saturn_V_aerial.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A Saturn V carrying\n         <a href="/wiki/Apollo_15" title="Apollo 15">\n          Apollo 15\n         </a>\n         rolls out to Pad 39A in 1971 on\n         <a href="/wiki/Mobile_Launcher_Platform_1" title="Mobile Launcher Platform 1">\n          Mobile Launch Platform 1\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       From 1967 through 1973, there were 13 Saturn V launches, including the ten remaining Apollo missions after Apollo 7. The first of two unmanned flights,\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_4" title="Apollo 4">\n        Apollo 4\n       </a>\n       (Apollo-Saturn 501) on November 9, 1967, was also the first rocket launch from KSC. The Saturn V\'s first manned launch on December 21, 1968 was\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_8" title="Apollo 8">\n        Apollo 8\n       </a>\n       \'s lunar orbiting mission. The next two missions tested the\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Lunar_Module" title="Apollo Lunar Module">\n        Lunar Module\n       </a>\n       :\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_9" title="Apollo 9">\n        Apollo 9\n       </a>\n       (Earth orbit) and\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_10" title="Apollo 10">\n        Apollo 10\n       </a>\n       (lunar orbit).\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_11" title="Apollo 11">\n        Apollo 11\n       </a>\n       , launched from Pad A on July 16, 1969, made the first Moon landing on July 20.\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_12" title="Apollo 12">\n        Apollo 12\n       </a>\n       followed four months later. From 1970\xe2\x80\x931972, the Apollo program concluded at KSC with the launches of missions 13 through 17.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Skylab">\n        Skylab\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Skylab">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       On May 14, 1973, the last\n       <a href="/wiki/Saturn_V" title="Saturn V">\n        Saturn V\n       </a>\n       launch put the\n       <a href="/wiki/Skylab" title="Skylab">\n        Skylab\n       </a>\n       space station in orbit from Pad 39A. By this time, the Cape Kennedy pads 34 and 37 used for the Saturn IB were decommissioned, and Pad B was modified to launch three manned missions to Skylab that year, as well as the final Apollo spacecraft for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo%E2%80%93Soyuz_Test_Project" title="Apollo\xe2\x80\x93Soyuz Test Project">\n        Apollo\xe2\x80\x93Soyuz Test Project\n       </a>\n       in 1975.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Space_Shuttle">\n        Space Shuttle\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Space Shuttle">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_program" title="Space Shuttle program">\n        Space Shuttle program\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_space_shuttle_missions" title="List of space shuttle missions">\n        List of space shuttle missions\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-60_Launch.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="551" data-file-width="700" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/STS-60_Launch.jpg/220px-STS-60_Launch.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/STS-60_Launch.jpg/330px-STS-60_Launch.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/STS-60_Launch.jpg/440px-STS-60_Launch.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-60_Launch.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Discovery" title="Space Shuttle Discovery">\n          Shuttle\n          <i>\n           Discovery\n          </i>\n         </a>\n         launching from Pad 39A on\n         <a href="/wiki/STS-60" title="STS-60">\n          STS-60\n         </a>\n         , February 3, 1994\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       As the Space Shuttle was being designed, NASA received proposals for building alternative launch-and-landing sites at locations other than KSC, which demanded study. KSC had important advantages, including: its existing facilities; location on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Intracoastal_Waterway" title="Intracoastal Waterway">\n        Intracoastal Waterway\n       </a>\n       ; and its southern latitude, which gives a velocity advantage to missions launched in easterly near-equatorial orbits. Disadvantages included: its inability to safely launch military missions into\n       <a href="/wiki/Polar_orbit" title="Polar orbit">\n        polar orbit\n       </a>\n       , since spent boosters would be likely to fall on the Carolinas or Cuba; corrosion from the salt air; and frequent cloudy or stormy weather. Although building a new site at\n       <a href="/wiki/White_Sands_Missile_Range" title="White Sands Missile Range">\n        White Sands Missile Range\n       </a>\n       in New Mexico was seriously considered, NASA announced its decision in April 1972 to use KSC for the shuttle.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-heppenheimer1998_16-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-heppenheimer1998-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Since the Shuttle could not be landed automatically or by remote control, the launch of\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia" title="Space Shuttle Columbia">\n         Columbia\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       on April 12, 1981 for its first orbital mission\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-1" title="STS-1">\n        STS-1\n       </a>\n       , was NASA\'s first manned launch of a vehicle that had not been tested in prior unmanned launches.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-36_Rollout_-_GPN-2000-000680.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2400" data-file-width="3000" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/STS-36_Rollout_-_GPN-2000-000680.jpg/220px-STS-36_Rollout_-_GPN-2000-000680.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/STS-36_Rollout_-_GPN-2000-000680.jpg/330px-STS-36_Rollout_-_GPN-2000-000680.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/STS-36_Rollout_-_GPN-2000-000680.jpg/440px-STS-36_Rollout_-_GPN-2000-000680.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-36_Rollout_-_GPN-2000-000680.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Atlantis" title="Space Shuttle Atlantis">\n          Shuttle\n          <i>\n           Atlantis\n          </i>\n         </a>\n         is moved to Pad 39A for the 1990 launch of\n         <a href="/wiki/STS-36" title="STS-36">\n          STS-36\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In 1976, the VAB\'s south parking area was the site of Third Century America, a science and technology display commemorating the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Bicentennial" title="U.S. Bicentennial">\n        U.S. Bicentennial\n       </a>\n       . Concurrent with this event, the U.S. flag was painted on the south side of the VAB. During the late 1970s, LC-39 was reconfigured to support the Space Shuttle. Two\n       <a href="/wiki/Orbiter_Processing_Facility" title="Orbiter Processing Facility">\n        Orbiter Processing Facilities\n       </a>\n       were built near the VAB as hangars with a third added in the 1980s.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       KSC\'s 2.9-mile (4.7\xc2\xa0km)\n       <a href="/wiki/Shuttle_Landing_Facility" title="Shuttle Landing Facility">\n        Shuttle Landing Facility\n       </a>\n       (SLF) was the orbiters\' primary end-of-mission landing site, although the first KSC landing did not take place until the tenth flight, when\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger" title="Space Shuttle Challenger">\n         Challenger\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       completed\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-41-B" title="STS-41-B">\n        STS-41-B\n       </a>\n       on February 11, 1984; the primary landing site until then was\n       <a href="/wiki/Edwards_Air_Force_Base" title="Edwards Air Force Base">\n        Edwards Air Force Base\n       </a>\n       in California, subsequently used as a backup landing site. The SLF also provided a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Return_To_Launch_Site" title="Return To Launch Site">\n        return-to-launch-site (RTLS) abort\n       </a>\n       option, which was not utilized. The SLF is among the longest runways in the world.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       After 24 successful shuttle flights,\n       <i>\n        Challenger\n       </i>\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Challenger disaster">\n        was torn apart\n       </a>\n       73 seconds after the launch of\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-51-L" title="STS-51-L">\n        STS-51-L\n       </a>\n       on January 28, 1986; the first shuttle launch from Pad 39B and the first U.S. manned launch failure, killing the seven crew members. An\n       <a href="/wiki/O-ring" title="O-ring">\n        O-ring\n       </a>\n       seal in the right booster rocket failed at liftoff, leading to subsequent structural failures. Flights resumed on September 29, 1988 with\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-26" title="STS-26">\n        STS-26\n       </a>\n       after modifications to many aspects of the shuttle program.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On February 1, 2003,\n       <i>\n        Columbia\n       </i>\n       and her crew of seven were lost during\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Re-entry" title="Re-entry">\n        re-entry\n       </a>\n       over Texas during the\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-107" title="STS-107">\n        STS-107\n       </a>\n       mission (the 113th shuttle flight); a vehicle breakup triggered by damage sustained during launch from Pad 39A on January 16, when a piece of foam insulation from the orbiter\'s external fuel tank struck the orbiter\'s left wing. During reentry, the damage created a hole allowing hot gases to melt the wing structure. Like the\n       <i>\n        Challenger\n       </i>\n       disaster, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Columbia disaster">\n        resulting investigation and modifications\n       </a>\n       interrupted shuttle flight operations at KSC for more than two years until the\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-114" title="STS-114">\n        STS-114\n       </a>\n       launch on July 26, 2005.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The shuttle program experienced five\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Main_Engine" title="Space Shuttle Main Engine">\n        main engine\n       </a>\n       shutdowns at LC-39, all within four seconds before launch; and one\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abort_to_Orbit" title="Abort to Orbit">\n        abort to orbit\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-51-F" title="STS-51-F">\n        STS-51-F\n       </a>\n       on July 29, 1985. Shuttle missions during nearly 30 years of operations included deploying satellites and interplanetary probes, conducting space science and technology experiments,\n       <a href="/wiki/Shuttle%E2%80%93Mir_Program" title="Shuttle\xe2\x80\x93Mir Program">\n        visits to the Russian MIR space station\n       </a>\n       , construction and servicing of the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       , deployment and servicing of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">\n        Hubble Space Telescope\n       </a>\n       and serving as a\n       <a href="/wiki/Spacelab" title="Spacelab">\n        space laboratory\n       </a>\n       . The shuttle was retired from service in July 2011 after 135 launches.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Constellation">\n        Constellation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Constellation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       On October 28, 2009, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ares_I-X" title="Ares I-X">\n        Ares I-X\n       </a>\n       launch from Pad 39B was the first unmanned launch from KSC since the Skylab workshop in 1973.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Expendable_launch_vehicles_(ELVs)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Expendable_launch_vehicles_.28ELVs.29">\n        Expendable launch vehicles (ELVs)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Expendable launch vehicles (ELVs)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Beginning in 1958, NASA and military worked side by side on robotic mission launches (previously referred to as unmanned),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       cooperating as they broke ground in the field. In the early 1960s, NASA had as many as two robotic mission launches a month. The frequent number of flights allowed for quick evolution of the vehicles, as engineers gathered data, learned from anomalies and implemented upgrades. In 1963, with the intent of KSC\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Expendable_launch_vehicle" title="Expendable launch vehicle">\n        ELV\n       </a>\n       work focusing on the ground support equipment and facilities, a separate Atlas/Centaur organization was formed under NASA\'s Lewis Center (now\n       <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Research_Center" title="Glenn Research Center">\n        Glenn Research Center (GRC)\n       </a>\n       ), taking that responsibility from the Launch Operations Center (aka KSC).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lipartito_6-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Lipartito-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Though almost all robotics missions launched from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Canaveral_Air_Force_Station" title="Cape Canaveral Air Force Station">\n        Cape Canaveral Air Force Station\n       </a>\n       (CCAFS), KSC "oversaw the final assembly and testing of rockets as they arrived at the Cape."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lipartito_6-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Lipartito-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 1965, KSC\'s Unmanned Launch Operations directorate became responsible all NASA unmanned launch operations, including those at\n       <a href="/wiki/Vandenberg_Air_Force_Base" title="Vandenberg Air Force Base">\n        Vandenberg Air Force Base\n       </a>\n       . From the 1950s to 1978, KSC chose the rocket and payload processing facilities for all robotic missions launching in the U.S., overseeing their near launch processing and checkout. In addition to government missions, KSC performed this service for commercial and foreign missions also, though non-U.S. government entities provided reimbursement. NASA also funded CCAFS launch pad maintenance and launch vehicle improvements.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       All this changed with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Space_Launch_Act_of_1984" title="Commercial Space Launch Act of 1984">\n        Commercial Space Launch Act of 1984\n       </a>\n       , after which NASA only coordinated its own and\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration" title="National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration">\n        National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration\n       </a>\n       (NOAA) ELV launches. Companies were able to "operate their own launch vehicles"\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lipartito_6-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Lipartito-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and utilize NASA\'s launch facilities. Payload processing handled by private firms also started to occur outside of KSC. Reagan\'s 1988 space policy furthered the movement of this work from KSC to commercial companies.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       That same year, launch complexes on CCAFS started transferring from NASA to air force management.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lipartito_6-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Lipartito-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the 1990s, though KSC was not performing the hands-on ELV work, engineers still maintained understanding of ELVs and had contracts allowing them insight in the vehicles so they could provide knowledgeable oversight. KSC also worked on ELV research and analysis and the contractors were able to utilize KSC personnel as a resource for technical issues. KSC, with the payload and launch vehicle industries, developed advances in automation of the ELV launch and ground operations for the purpose of enabling competitiveness of U.S. rockets against the global market.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lipartito_6-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Lipartito-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1998, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Launch_Services_Program" title="Launch Services Program">\n        Launch Services Program\n       </a>\n       (LSP) formed at KSC, pulling together programs (and personnel) that already existed at KSC, GRC,\n       <a href="/wiki/Goddard_Space_Flight_Center" title="Goddard Space Flight Center">\n        Goddard Space Flight Center\n       </a>\n       , and more to manage the launch of NASA and NOAA robotic missions. CCAFS and VAFB are the primary launch sites for LSP missions, though other sites are occasionally used. LSP payloads such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars_Science_Laboratory" title="Mars Science Laboratory">\n        Mars Science Laboratory\n       </a>\n       have been processed at KSC before being transferred to a launch pad on CCAFS.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Space_station_processing">\n        Space station processing\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Space station processing">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       As the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       modules design began in the early 1990s, KSC began to work with other NASA centers and international partners to prepare for processing prior to launch on board the Space Shuttles. KSC utilized its hands-on experience processing the 22\n       <a href="/wiki/Spacelab" title="Spacelab">\n        Spacelab\n       </a>\n       missions in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Operations_and_Checkout_Building" title="Operations and Checkout Building">\n        Operations and Checkout Building\n       </a>\n       to gather expectations of ISS processing. These experiences were incorporated into the design of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Station_Processing_Facility" title="Space Station Processing Facility">\n        Space Station Processing Facility\n       </a>\n       (SSPF), which began construction in 1993. The Space Station Directorate formed in 1996. KSC personnel were embedded at station module factories for insight into their processes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lipartito_6-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Lipartito-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       From 1997 to 2007, KSC planned and performed\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Station_Processing_Facility#Station_Integration_Testing" title="Space Station Processing Facility">\n        on the ground integration tests and checkouts of station modules\n       </a>\n       : three Multi-Element Integration Testing (MEIT) sessions and the Integration Systems Test (IST). Numerous issues were found and corrected that would have been difficult to nearly impossible to do on-orbit.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Today KSC continues to process ISS payloads from across the world prior to launch along with developing its own experiments for on orbit.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISS_Payloads_20-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ISS_Payloads-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Current_programs_and_initiatives">\n        Current programs and initiatives\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Current programs and initiatives">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The following are current programs and initiatives at Kennedy Space Center:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA_KSC_Home_21-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NASA_KSC_Home-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commercial_Crew_Program" title="Commercial Crew Program">\n         Commercial Crew Program\n        </a>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n         <a href="#cite_note-22">\n          [22]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Ground Systems Development and Operations Program\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">\n         <a href="#cite_note-23">\n          [23]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <ul>\n         <li>\n          NASA is currently designing the next heavy launch vehicle known as the\n          <a href="/wiki/Space_Launch_System" title="Space Launch System">\n           Space Launch System (SLS)\n          </a>\n          for continuation of human spaceflight.\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          On December 5, 2014, NASA launched the first unmanned flight test of the\n          <a href="/wiki/Orion_(spacecraft)" title="Orion (spacecraft)">\n           Orion Multi-Purpose Crew Vehicle\n          </a>\n          (MPCV), currently under development to facilitate human exploration of the\n          <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">\n           Moon\n          </a>\n          ,\n          <a href="/wiki/Asteroid" title="Asteroid">\n           asteroids\n          </a>\n          , and\n          <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">\n           Mars\n          </a>\n          .\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n           <a href="#cite_note-24">\n            [24]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">\n           <a href="#cite_note-25">\n            [25]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </li>\n        </ul>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Launch_Services_Program" title="Launch Services Program">\n         Launch Services Program\n        </a>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n         <a href="#cite_note-26">\n          [26]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Launch_Services_Program#CubeSats" title="Launch Services Program">\n         Educational Launch of Nanosatellites (ELaNa)\n        </a>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n         <a href="#cite_note-27">\n          [27]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Research and Technology\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Research_.26_Tech_7-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Research_.26_Tech-7">\n          [7]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n         International Space Station\n        </a>\n        Payloads\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISS_Payloads_20-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-ISS_Payloads-20">\n          [20]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Facilities">\n        Facilities\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Facilities">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The KSC Industrial Area, where many of the center\'s support facilities are located, is 5 miles (8\xc2\xa0km) south of LC-39. It includes the\n       <a href="/wiki/KSC_Headquarters_Building" title="KSC Headquarters Building">\n        Headquarters Building\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Operations_and_Checkout_Building" title="Operations and Checkout Building">\n        Operations and Checkout Building\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Central_Instrumentation_Facility" title="Central Instrumentation Facility">\n        Central Instrumentation Facility\n       </a>\n       . The astronaut crew quarters are in the O&amp;C; before it was completed, the astronaut crew quarters were located in Hangar S\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       at the Cape Canaveral Missile Test Annex (now\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Canaveral_Air_Force_Station" title="Cape Canaveral Air Force Station">\n        CCAFS\n       </a>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KSC_History_Quiz_12-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-KSC_History_Quiz-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Located as KSC was the\n       <a href="/wiki/Merritt_Island_Spaceflight_Tracking_and_Data_Network_station" title="Merritt Island Spaceflight Tracking and Data Network station">\n        Merritt Island Spaceflight Tracking and Data Network station\n       </a>\n       (MILA), a key radio communications and spacecraft tracking complex.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Kennedy_Space_Center.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1166" data-file-width="1547" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Map_of_Kennedy_Space_Center.png/220px-Map_of_Kennedy_Space_Center.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Map_of_Kennedy_Space_Center.png/330px-Map_of_Kennedy_Space_Center.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Map_of_Kennedy_Space_Center.png/440px-Map_of_Kennedy_Space_Center.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Kennedy_Space_Center.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Official visitor map of KSC industrial area\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Facilities at the Kennedy Space Center are directly related to its mission to launch and, in some cases, recover missions. Facilities are available to prepare and maintain spacecraft and payloads for flight.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">\n        <a href="#cite_note-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Headquarters (HQ) Building houses offices for the Center Director, library, film and photo archives, a print shop and security.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">\n        <a href="#cite_note-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A new Headquarters Building is under construction as a part of the Central Campus consolidation and the first phase is expected to be complete in 2017.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Master_Plan_2012_9-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Master_Plan_2012-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n        <a href="#cite_note-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The center operated its own 17-mile (27\xc2\xa0km)\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA_Railroad" title="NASA Railroad">\n        short-line railroad\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This operation was discontinued in 2015, with the sale of its final two locomotives. A third had already been donated to a museum. The line was costing $1.3 million annually to maintain.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Payload_processing">\n        Payload processing\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Payload processing">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        Payloads are received, processed and integrated together in the\n        <a href="/wiki/Operations_and_Checkout_Building" title="Operations and Checkout Building">\n         Operations and Checkout Building\n        </a>\n        (O&amp;C) dating back to the 1960s with the Gemini and Apollo programs, 70s with the Skylab program and 80s and 90s for initial segments of the International Space Station.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n         <a href="#cite_note-37">\n          [37]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The three-story, 457,000 square feet (42,500\xc2\xa0m\n        <sup>\n         2\n        </sup>\n        )\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Station_Processing_Facility" title="Space Station Processing Facility">\n         Space Station Processing Facility\n        </a>\n        (SSPF) consists of two processing bays, an airlock, operational control rooms, laboratories, logistics areas and office space for support of non-hazardous Station and Shuttle payloads to\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Class_3000" title="Class 3000">\n         ISO 14644-1 class 5\n        </a>\n        standards.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n         <a href="#cite_note-38">\n          [38]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The Vertical Processing Facility (VPF) features a 71 feet (22\xc2\xa0m) x 38 feet (12\xc2\xa0m) door where payloads which are processed in the vertical position are brought in and manipulated with two overhead cranes and a hoist capable of lifting up to 35 short tons (32\xc2\xa0t).\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n         <a href="#cite_note-39">\n          [39]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The Hypergolic Maintenance and Checkout Area (HMCA) comprises three buildings which are isolated from the rest of the industrial area because of the hazardous materials handled there.\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hypergolic-fuel" title="Hypergolic-fuel">\n         Hypergolic-fueled\n        </a>\n        modules that made up the Space Shuttle Orbiter\'s\n        <a href="/wiki/Reaction_control_system" title="Reaction control system">\n         reaction control system\n        </a>\n        , orbital maneuvering system and auxiliary power units were stored and serviced in the HMCF.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n         <a href="#cite_note-40">\n          [40]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Launch_Complex_39">\n        Launch Complex 39\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Launch Complex 39">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39" title="Kennedy Space Center Launch Complex 39">\n        Kennedy Space Center Launch Complex 39\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aerial_View_of_Launch_Complex_39.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1914" data-file-width="3000" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Aerial_View_of_Launch_Complex_39.jpg/220px-Aerial_View_of_Launch_Complex_39.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Aerial_View_of_Launch_Complex_39.jpg/330px-Aerial_View_of_Launch_Complex_39.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Aerial_View_of_Launch_Complex_39.jpg/440px-Aerial_View_of_Launch_Complex_39.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aerial_View_of_Launch_Complex_39.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The\n         <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_Assembly_Building" title="Vehicle Assembly Building">\n          Vehicle Assembly Building\n         </a>\n         (center) in 1999, with the\n         <a href="/wiki/Launch_Control_Center" title="Launch Control Center">\n          Launch Control Center\n         </a>\n         jutting out from its right, and Pads A and B in the distance\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39" title="Kennedy Space Center Launch Complex 39">\n        Launch Complex 39\n       </a>\n       (LC-39) was originally built for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Saturn_V" title="Saturn V">\n        Saturn V\n       </a>\n       , the largest and most powerful operational launch vehicle in history, for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">\n        Apollo manned Moon landing program\n       </a>\n       . Since the end of the Apollo program in 1972, LC-39 has been used to launch every NASA human space flight, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Skylab" title="Skylab">\n        Skylab\n       </a>\n       (1973), the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apollo-Soyuz_Test_Project" title="Apollo-Soyuz Test Project">\n        Apollo-Soyuz Test Project\n       </a>\n       (1975), and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_program" title="Space Shuttle program">\n        Space Shuttle program\n       </a>\n       (1981-2011).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Since December 1968, all launch operations have been conducted from\n       <a href="/wiki/Launch_pad" title="Launch pad">\n        launch pads\n       </a>\n       A and B at LC-39. Both pads are on the ocean, 3 miles (4.8\xc2\xa0km) east of the VAB. From 1969\xe2\x80\x931972, LC-39 was the departure point for all six\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">\n        Apollo\n       </a>\n       manned Moon landing missions using the\n       <a href="/wiki/Saturn_V" title="Saturn V">\n        Saturn V\n       </a>\n       , and was used from 1981\xe2\x80\x932011 for all\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n        Space Shuttle\n       </a>\n       launches.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Human missions to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">\n        Moon\n       </a>\n       required the large three-stage Saturn V rocket, which was 363 feet (111 meters) tall and 33 feet (10 meters) in diameter. At KSC,\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39" title="Kennedy Space Center Launch Complex 39">\n        Launch Complex 39\n       </a>\n       (LC-39) was built on Merritt Island to accommodate the new rocket. Construction of the $800\xc2\xa0million project began in November 1962. LC-39 pads A and B were completed by October 1965 (planned Pads C, D and E were canceled), the VAB was completed in June 1965, and the infrastructure by late 1966.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The complex includes:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        the\n        <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_Assembly_Building" title="Vehicle Assembly Building">\n         Vehicle Assembly Building\n        </a>\n        (VAB), a 130,000,000 cubic feet (3,700,000\xc2\xa0m\n        <sup>\n         3\n        </sup>\n        ) hangar capable of holding four Saturn Vs. The VAB is the fourth-largest structure in the world by volume, and was the largest when completed in 1965.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-congressional_record_Sep_8.2C_2004_41-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-congressional_record_Sep_8.2C_2004-41">\n          [41]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        a\n        <a href="/wiki/Crawler-transporter" title="Crawler-transporter">\n         transporter\n        </a>\n        capable of carrying 5,440 tons along a\n        <a href="/wiki/Crawlerway" title="Crawlerway">\n         crawlerway\n        </a>\n        to either of two launch pads;\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        a 446-foot (136\xc2\xa0m) mobile\n        <a href="/wiki/Service_structure" title="Service structure">\n         service structure\n        </a>\n        , with three\n        <a href="/wiki/Mobile_Launcher_Platform" title="Mobile Launcher Platform">\n         Mobile Launcher Platforms\n        </a>\n        , each containing a fixed launch umbilical tower;\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        the\n        <a href="/wiki/Launch_Control_Center" title="Launch Control Center">\n         Launch Control Center\n        </a>\n        ; and\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        a\n        <a href="/wiki/Launch_Complex_39_Press_Site" title="Launch Complex 39 Press Site">\n         news media facility\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_leasing">\n        Commercial leasing\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Commercial leasing">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       As a part of promoting commercial space industry growth in the area and the overall center as a multi-user spaceport,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       KSC leases some of its properties. Here are some major examples:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Exploration_Park" title="Exploration Park">\n         Exploration Park\n        </a>\n        to multiple users (partnership with\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Florida" title="Space Florida">\n         Space Florida\n        </a>\n        )\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Shuttle_Landing_Facility" title="Shuttle Landing Facility">\n         Shuttle Landing Facility\n        </a>\n        to\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Florida" title="Space Florida">\n         Space Florida\n        </a>\n        (who contracts use to private companies)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Orbiter_Processing_Facility#Orbiter_assignments.2FOPF_status" title="Orbiter Processing Facility">\n         Orbiter Processing Facility (OPF)-3\n        </a>\n        to\n        <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">\n         Boeing\n        </a>\n        (for\n        <a href="/wiki/CST-100_Starliner" title="CST-100 Starliner">\n         CST-100 Starliner\n        </a>\n        )\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39#Launch_Pad_39A" title="Kennedy Space Center Launch Complex 39">\n         LC-39A\n        </a>\n        to\n        <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">\n         SpaceX\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Operations_and_Checkout_Building" title="Operations and Checkout Building">\n         O&amp;C High Bay\n        </a>\n        to\n        <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin" title="Lockheed Martin">\n         Lockheed Martin\n        </a>\n        (for\n        <a href="/wiki/Orion_(spacecraft)" title="Orion (spacecraft)">\n         Orion\n        </a>\n        processing)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Land for FPL\xe2\x80\x99s\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Coast_Next_Generation_Solar_Energy_Center" title="Space Coast Next Generation Solar Energy Center">\n         Space Coast Next Generation Solar Energy Center\n        </a>\n        to\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Florida_Power_and_Light" title="Florida Power and Light">\n         Florida Power and Light\n        </a>\n        (FPL)\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">\n         <a href="#cite_note-44">\n          [44]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n         <a href="#cite_note-45">\n          [45]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">\n         <a href="#cite_note-46">\n          [46]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Hypergolic Maintenance Facility (HMF) to United Paradyne Corporation (UPC)\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n         <a href="#cite_note-47">\n          [47]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Visitor_complex">\n        Visitor complex\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Visitor complex">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center_Visitor_Complex" title="Kennedy Space Center Visitor Complex">\n        Kennedy Space Center Visitor Complex\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:KennedySpaceCentreVisitor%27sCentreFrontGate.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/KennedySpaceCentreVisitor%27sCentreFrontGate.JPG/220px-KennedySpaceCentreVisitor%27sCentreFrontGate.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/KennedySpaceCentreVisitor%27sCentreFrontGate.JPG/330px-KennedySpaceCentreVisitor%27sCentreFrontGate.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/KennedySpaceCentreVisitor%27sCentreFrontGate.JPG/440px-KennedySpaceCentreVisitor%27sCentreFrontGate.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:KennedySpaceCentreVisitor%27sCentreFrontGate.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Gate to the KSC Visitor Complex in 2006;\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Explorer" title="Space Shuttle Explorer">\n          <i>\n           Explorer\n          </i>\n         </a>\n         , a\n         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n          Space Shuttle\n         </a>\n         mock-up, is in the background\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Kennedy Space Center Visitor Complex, operated by\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_North" title="Delaware North">\n        Delaware North\n       </a>\n       since 1995, has a variety of exhibits, artifacts, displays and attractions on the history and future of human and robotic spaceflight. Bus tours of KSC originate from here. The complex also includes the separate\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apollo/Saturn_V_Center" title="Apollo/Saturn V Center">\n        Apollo/Saturn V Center\n       </a>\n       , north of the VAB and the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Astronaut_Hall_of_Fame" title="United States Astronaut Hall of Fame">\n        United States Astronaut Hall of Fame\n       </a>\n       , six miles west near\n       <a href="/wiki/Titusville,_Florida" title="Titusville, Florida">\n        Titusville\n       </a>\n       . There were 1.5\xc2\xa0million visitors in 2009. It had some 700 employees.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">\n        <a href="#cite_note-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       It was announced on May 29, 2015 that the Astronaut Hall of Fame exhibit would be moved from its current location to another location within the Visitor Complex to make room for an upcoming high-tech attraction entitled "Heroes and Legends". The attraction, to be designed by Orlando-based design firm Falcon\'s Treehouse, is slated to open sometime late 2016.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">\n        <a href="#cite_note-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In March 2016, the visitor center unveiled the new location of the iconic countdown clock at the complex\'s entrance; previously, the clock was located with a flagpole at the press site. The clock was originally built and installed in 1969 and listed with the flagpole in the National Register of Historic Places in January 2000.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n        <a href="#cite_note-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Historic_locations">\n        Historic locations\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Historic locations">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       NASA lists the following Historic Districts at KSC; each district has multiple associated facilities:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Historic_Sites_51-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Historic_Sites-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n        <a href="#cite_note-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n        <a href="#cite_note-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        Launch Complex 39: Pad A Historic District\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Launch Complex 39: Pad B Historic District\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Shuttle_Landing_Facility" title="Shuttle Landing Facility">\n         Shuttle Landing Facility\n        </a>\n        (SLF) Area Historic District\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Orbiter Processing Historic District\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Solid Rocket Booster (SRB) Disassembly and Refurbishment Complex Historic District\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        NASA KSC Railroad System Historic District\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        NASA-owned Cape Canaveral Air Force Station Industrial Area Historic District\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       There are 24 historic properties outside of these historic districts, including the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Atlantis" title="Space Shuttle Atlantis">\n         Space Shuttle Atlantis\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_Assembly_Building" title="Vehicle Assembly Building">\n        Vehicle Assembly Building\n       </a>\n       , Crawlerway, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Operations_and_Checkout_Building" title="Operations and Checkout Building">\n        Operations and Checkout Building\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Historic_Sites_51-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Historic_Sites-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       KSC has one\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Historic_Landmark" title="National Historic Landmark">\n        National Historic Landmark\n       </a>\n       , 78\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">\n        National Register of Historic Places\n       </a>\n       (NRHP) listed or eligible sites, and 100 Archaeological Sites.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">\n        <a href="#cite_note-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Further information:\n       <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_Space_Center_MPS" title="John F. Kennedy Space Center MPS">\n        John F. Kennedy Space Center MPS\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Weather">\n        Weather\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Weather">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mercury-Redstone_display_toppled_KSC-04PD-1721.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Mercury-Redstone_display_toppled_KSC-04PD-1721.jpg/220px-Mercury-Redstone_display_toppled_KSC-04PD-1721.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Mercury-Redstone_display_toppled_KSC-04PD-1721.jpg/330px-Mercury-Redstone_display_toppled_KSC-04PD-1721.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Mercury-Redstone_display_toppled_KSC-04PD-1721.jpg/440px-Mercury-Redstone_display_toppled_KSC-04PD-1721.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mercury-Redstone_display_toppled_KSC-04PD-1721.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A Mercury Redstone rocket on display at Gate 3 was toppled by Hurricane Frances on September 7, 2004.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Florida\'s peninsular shape and temperature contrasts between land and ocean provide ideal conditions for electrical storms, earning Central Florida the reputation as "lightning capital of the United States".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-climatology_55-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-climatology-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lightning_FAQ_56-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Lightning_FAQ-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This makes extensive\n       <a href="/wiki/Lightning" title="Lightning">\n        lightning\n       </a>\n       protection and detection systems necessary to protect employees, structures and spacecraft on launch pads.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">\n        <a href="#cite_note-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On November 14, 1969,\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_12" title="Apollo 12">\n        Apollo 12\n       </a>\n       was struck by lightning just after lift-off from Pad 39A, but the flight continued safely. The most powerful lightning strike recorded at KSC occurred at LC-39B on August 25, 2006, while\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Atlantis" title="Space Shuttle Atlantis">\n        shuttle\n        <i>\n         Atlantis\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       was being prepared for\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-115" title="STS-115">\n        STS-115\n       </a>\n       . NASA managers were initially concerned that the lightning strike caused damage to\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       , but none was found.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n        <a href="#cite_note-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On September 7, 2004,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Frances" title="Hurricane Frances">\n        Hurricane Frances\n       </a>\n       directly hit the area with sustained winds of 70 miles per hour (110\xc2\xa0km/h) and gusts up to 94 miles per hour (151\xc2\xa0km/h), the most damaging storm to date. The Vehicle Assembly Building lost 1,000 exterior panels, each 3.9 feet (1.2\xc2\xa0m) x 9.8 feet (3.0\xc2\xa0m) in size. This exposed 39,800\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0ft (3,700\xc2\xa0m\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) of the building to the elements. Damage occurred to the south and east sides of the VAB. The shuttle\'s Thermal Protection System Facility suffered extensive damage. The roof was partially torn off and the interior suffered water damage. Several rockets on display in the center were toppled.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RELEASE_:_04-288_59-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-RELEASE_:_04-288-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Further damage to KSC was caused by\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Wilma" title="Hurricane Wilma">\n        Hurricane Wilma\n       </a>\n       in October 2005.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="KSC_directors">\n        KSC directors\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: KSC directors">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kurt_H._Debus.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2187" data-file-width="1752" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Kurt_H._Debus.jpg/170px-Kurt_H._Debus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Kurt_H._Debus.jpg/255px-Kurt_H._Debus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Kurt_H._Debus.jpg/340px-Kurt_H._Debus.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kurt_H._Debus.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Dr. Kurt Debus, first director of KSC\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Since KSC\'s formation, ten NASA officials have served as directors, including three former astronauts (Crippen, Bridges and Cabana):\n      </p>\n      <table Kennedy\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         August 9, 2003\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         January 2007\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">\n          <a href="#cite_note-67">\n           [67]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/William_W._Parsons_(NASA)" title="William W. Parsons (NASA)">\n          William W. Parsons\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         January 2007\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         October 2008\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n          <a href="#cite_note-68">\n           [68]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Robert_D._Cabana" title="Robert D. Cabana">\n          Robert D. Cabana\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         October 2008\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         present\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n          <a href="#cite_note-69">\n           [69]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Labor_force">\n        Labor force\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Labor force">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       When KSC separated from\n       <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Space_Flight_Center" title="Marshall Space Flight Center">\n        Marshall Space Flight Center\n       </a>\n       in July 1962, it took 375 employees with it.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In May 1965, KSC had 7,000 employees and contractors move from rented space in Cocoa Beach to the new Merritt Island facilities. The peak number of persons working on center was 26,000 in 1968 (3,000 were civil servants). In 1970,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/President_Nixon" title="President Nixon">\n        President Nixon\n       </a>\n       announced intent to reduce cost of space operations and major cuts occurred at KSC. By 1974, KSC\'s workforce was down to 10,000 employees (2,408 civil servants).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lipartito_6-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Lipartito-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A total of 13,100 people worked at the center as of 2011. Approximately 2,100 are employees of the federal government; the rest are contractors.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jdean_70-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-jdean-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The average annual salary for an on-site worker in 2008 was $77,235.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">\n        <a href="#cite_note-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The end of the Space Shuttle program in 2011, preceded by the cancellation of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constellation_Program" title="Constellation Program">\n        Constellation Program\n       </a>\n       in 2010, produced a significant downsizing of the KSC workforce similar to that experienced at the end of the Apollo program in 1972. As part of this downsizing, 6,000 contractors lost their jobs at the Center during 2010 and 2011.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">\n        <a href="#cite_note-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span
